      28             : /* The used range inference algorithm is described in:
      29             :  *     V. Campos, R. Rodrigues, I. de Assis Costa and F. Pereira.
      30             :  *     "Speed and Precision in Range Analysis", SBLP'12.
      31             :  *
      32             :  * There are a couple degrees of freedom, we use:
      33             :  *  * Propagation on SCCs.
      34             :  *  * e-SSA for live range splitting.
      35             :  *  * Only intra-procedural inference.
      36             :  *  * Widening with warmup passes, but without jump sets.
      37             :  */
      38             :

    3873             : 
    3874             : /* This function recursively checks whether it's possible to convert an integer variable
    3875             :  * initialization to a double initialization. The basic idea is that if the value is used
    3876             :  * only in add/sub/mul/div ("narrowable" instructions) with a double result value, then it
    3877             :  * will be cast to double at that point anyway, so we may as well do it earlier already.
    3878             :  *
    3879             :  * The tricky case are chains of operations, where it's not necessarily a given that converting
    3880             :  * an integer to double before the chain of operations is the same as converting it after the
    3881             :  * chain. What this function does is detect two cases where it is safe:
    3882             :  *  * If the operations only involve constants, then we can simply verify that performing the
    3883             :  *    calculation on integers and doubles yields the same value.
    3884             :  *  * Even if one operand is not known, we may be able to determine that the operations with the
    3885             :  *    integer replaced by a double only acts as an effective double cast on the unknown operand.
    3886             :  *    E.g. 0+$i and 0.0+$i only differ by that cast. If then the consuming instruction of this
    3887             :  *    result will perform a double cast anyway, the conversion is safe.
    3888             :  *
    3889             :  * The checks happens recursively, while keeping track of which variables are already visited to
    3890             :  * avoid infinite loops. An iterative, worklist driven approach would be possible, but the state
    3891             :  * management more cumbersome to implement, so we don't bother for now.
    3892             :  */
